17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                                                             Page ii
EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

The purpose of this study is to conduct an operational analysis of the east-west corridors of 17th
Street and Dade Boulevard in Miami Beach, Florida. The corridors were evaluated for
improvements in the traffic flow and roadway connectivity within the study limits. Critical
intersections with the east-west routes were analyzed for potential improvements.


Currently, the corridor segments bisect the West Avenue/Bay Road neighborhood on the north
and the Bayshore neighborhood on the south at 17th Street. The project is a continuation of the
feasibility study for providing a bridge over the Collins Canal to connect West Avenue to Dade
Boulevard. The bridge feasibility study considered the most viable options for bridge type,
constructability study and an evaluation of the potential costs associated with the construction of
the bridge. The traffic analysis evaluated the impacts to the surrounding neighborhood from
routing some of the traffic from the major north-south roadways, Alton Road, to West Avenue, a
local street. This study assessed the impacts that the proposed bridge connection would have
on the intersection of Dade Boulevard and Purdy Avenue in order to develop recommendations
for improvements.


Data collection efforts consisted of obtaining all relevant data pertaining to the existing corridors.
Relevant local agencies were contacted to solicit useful information or input. The project data
collection included the following: site visits, highway and land use characteristics, and traffic
data (turning movement counts, signal timing information, and travel time delay study).


Using the data and inventory collected, Level of Service (LOS) Analyses were performed for
existing conditions.   The analysis was assessed by using the accepted measure of
effectiveness for roadway congestion, Level of Service (LOS). LOS "D" (or better) is the desired
target to be achieved at both signalized intersections and corridors. The existing LOS was
calculated and analyzed using version (6) of Synchro for both weekday and weekend peak
periods.


During the weekday PM peak hour, the results showed that all signalized intersections were
operating at acceptable LOS. It also indicated that the majority of the failing movements
occurred along Alton Road at Dade Boulevard and at 17th Street intersections, in the east/west
direction. The EB right-turn also failed at Dade Boulevard and Bay Road. Only one southbound
movement (SB left-turn) fails at Alton Road and 17th Street intersection.


During the weekend peak period, the results showed that all signalized intersections were
operating at acceptable LOS. As with the weekday PM peak analysis, the majority of the failing
movements occurred along Alton Road at Dade Boulevard and at 17th Street intersections, in
the east/west direction. However, unlike the weekday PM peak analysis, there were no other
failing movements.



17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                              Page 1
The results of the existing weekday and weekend peak arterial LOS analysis along 17th Street
and Dade Boulevard Avenue indicated the following:

Weekday PM Peak
    17th Street ­ This link operates with an overall LOS F in both directions of travel.
    Dade Boulevard ­ The arterial segment is operating below acceptable LOS in the EB
      direction. In the WB direction, the overall LOS is D.

Weekend Peak
    17th Street ­ Similar to the weekday conditions, this link operates with LOS F in both
      directions of travel.
    Dade Boulevard ­ The arterial segment is operating operates with LOS E and F in the
      EB and WB directions of travel, respectively, with the WB direction operating worse
      than the weekday conditions.

The proposed project would create a bridge over Collins Canal, with an at-grade roadway
intersection between West Avenue and Dade Boulevard. Since the Collins Canal is considered
a non-navigable waterway, except for small crafts, the bridge design would result in a low-level
bridge with minimal vertical clearance similar to the existing bridges at Alton Road and at 17th
Street over the Canal. This bridge would consist of a two-span, concrete flat-slab, skewed
bridge approximately seventy-five feet (75') long. It would accommodate two 12' lanes, a 5'
bicycle lane on each side, a 5' sidewalk on each side with a 1'-1" pedestrian barrier on the
exterior edges, and 1'-6" traffic railing barriers separating the traffic from pedestrian traffic,
requiring approximately 49 feet, 2 inches across the bridge width. Traffic volumes were diverted
along Alton Road at critical intersections to the proposed West Avenue Bridge. Based on the
traffic volume diversion, arterial and intersection Level of Service (LOS) Analyses were
performed for the proposed bridge conditions.


The following signal improvements were included under the project scenario:
        West Avenue at 17th Street is proposed to operate as a four-leg operation with the
        proposed bridge connection on the SB approach. This intersection is recommended to
        continue operating under Control Section Number 274 and coordinated in the east/west
        direction.
        West Avenue at Dade Boulevard is proposed as a new signalized intersection,
        operating under Control Section Number 274 and coordinated in the east/west direction
        with a cycle length of 130 seconds for both weekday and weekend peak periods.
        Traffic optimization on coordinated sections consisted of holding the existing cycle
        length while optimizing the phasing splits and the offsets.            At uncoordinated
        intersections, optimization consisted of adjusting the phasing splits.

The results of the project weekday evening peak hour LOS analysis showed that all signalized
intersections would operate at acceptable LOS. Several movements would fail in the east,
west, and south directions at Dade Boulevard and West Avenue. Alton Road at 17th Street and
at Dade Boulevard would also report failing movements in the west direction. The southbound
left and through movements would fail at the intersection of 17th Street and West Avenue.

17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                          Page 2
Similar to the weekday conditions, the results of the project weekend peak hour LOS analysis
showed that all signalized intersections would be operating at acceptable LOS. However,
several movements would be failing in the east and west directions at Alton Road and 17th
Street and at Dade Boulevard. The east and southbound movements would fail at the
intersection of Dade Boulevard and West Avenue.


The results of the bridge project weekday and weekend peak arterial LOS analysis along 17th
Street and Dade Boulevard within the study limits are outlined below:


Weekday PM Peak
    17th Street ­ This link operates with LOS F in both directions of travel.
    Dade Boulevard ­ This segment operates with LOS F in both directions of travel, worse
      than with existing conditions. This is due to the introduction of the new signal at West
      Avenue, which does not help the traffic progression along the corridor.

Weekend Peak
    17th Street ­ As with existing conditions, this link operates with LOS F in both directions
      of travel. These results are also similar to the project weekday conditions.
    Dade Boulevard ­ Similar to existing conditions, the arterial segment is operating
      operates with LOS F and E in the EB and WB directions of travel, respectively.

A comparison of the intersection level of service analyses is summarized in the following table
below. The LOS improves slightly with the proposed bridge for the intersections along Dade
Boulevard at Bay Road and at Alton Road during the weekday PM peak hour. However, the
LOS slightly decreases at the intersection along West Avenue at Dade Boulevard and at 17th
Street during both peak periods. This is due to the introduction of the new signal at Dade
Boulevard and West Avenue and the new south approach at West Avenue and 17th Street.
Notwithstanding, all of the intersections are still operating at acceptable levels of service D or
better.

Dade Boulevard in the westbound direction during the weekend peak hour from a LOS F to E.
However, it is the reverse for the weekday PM peak hour, with the LOS decreasing from D to F
under the proposed bridge scenario. The LOS also decreases slightly from E to F with the

Based on the data collection and the analysis performed, the results indicate that the proposed
bridge crossing alone does not greatly improve the traffic operations for the east-west corridors.
Additional improvements consisting of modifications to the existing bridge and other critical
intersections will need to be evaluated further in order to maximize the benefits of the proposed
bridge.


In addition, safety for pedestrians and bicyclists, as well as vehicular traffic, may be improved
with the proposed bridge. A safety review of the critical intersections along Dade Boulevard
should be made in order to determine the extent of these benefits more accurately. Also, the
right-of-way requirements, as well as the roadway alignment, need to be evaluated further for
the east-west corridors. A benefit/cost analysis would also need to be conducted in order to
quantify the benefits of the proposed bridge connection for the east-west corridors.


A previous benefit/cost analysis, which evaluated the north-south corridors of West Avenue and
Alton Road, indicated that the construction of the proposed bridge was economically feasible.
Furthermore, the proposed bridge will provide a more direct connection to the Sunset
Neighborhood.




17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                                     Page 5
1.0 INTRODUCTION

The purpose of this study is to conduct an operational analysis of the east-west corridors of 17th
Street and Dade Boulevard in Miami Beach, Florida. The corridors were evaluated for
improvements in the traffic flow and roadway connectivity within the study limits. Critical
intersections with the east-west routes were analyzed for potential improvements.

Currently, the corridor segments bisect the West Avenue/Bay Road neighborhood on the north
and the Bayshore neighborhood on the south at 17th Street. The project is a continuation of the
feasibility study for providing a bridge over the Collins Canal to connect West Avenue to Dade
Boulevard. The bridge feasibility study considered the most viable options for bridge type,
constructability study and an evaluation of the potential costs associated with the construction of
the bridge. The traffic analysis evaluated the impacts to the surrounding neighborhood from
routing some of the traffic from the major north-south roadways, Alton Road, to West Avenue, a
local street. This study will assess the impacts that the proposed bridge connection will have on
the intersection of Dade Boulevard and Purdy Avenue in order to develop recommendations for
improvements. The study corridors are shown in Figure 1.


                                       Figure 1. Study Area




17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                           Page 6
2.0 DATA COLLECTION

Data collection efforts consisted of obtaining all relevant data pertaining to the existing corridors.
Relevant local agencies were contacted to solicit useful information or input. The project data
collection is summarized in the following sections.


2.1   Site Visits
A site visit of the intersection at Dade Boulevard and Purdy Avenue was conducted in order to
collect information on intersection geometry and lane use/arrangements, and identify existing
traffic control devices including pedestrian features, and other roadway or roadside elements
such as the location of bus stops, on-street parking, and driveways. A photographic log of the
field review is included in Appendix A.


A site visit of the study corridors was also conducted to observe the traffic operations in the
east-west directions. These observations were used to calibrate and validate the existing model
for the east-west corridor movements. The site visits were conducted during the peak hour
during both peak periods as identified in the previous study.


2.2   Highway and Land Use Characteristics
Relevant data was obtained from various sources, such as the City of Miami Beach, the Florida
Department of Transportation, and local utility companies. This information served as the basis
for evaluation, as well as on-site inventory and verification of existing data.


Currently, the existing zoning of the area north of Dade Boulevard, namely the Sunset Harbor
neighborhood, is designated as I-1 or Light Industrial consisting of residential uses in the
northwest periphery, commercial and industrial in the core, while the southwest periphery is for
government use. The major traffic generator in the area is a Publix supermarket located in the
northwest portion of the neighborhood.


The intersection lane use geometry is presented in Figure 2. A description of the major routes
within the study area is presented below:




17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                              Page 7
                            Figure 2. Intersection Lane Use Geometry




17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                      Page 8
           Dade Boulevard is an east/west urban minor arterial road 3.80 miles in length. Within
           the study limits, this is a four-lane undivided road with a posted speed limit of 35 MPH
           spanning approximately 1,400 feet (0.26 miles) in length from Purdy Avenue to Alton
           Road. Sidewalks are present on the north side of the entire segment and only on the
           south side east of Purdy Avenue. On-street parking is not allowed. There is a bicycle
           lane, recently added in the last year along this segment, which starts from the Venetian
           Causeway and terminates at Dade Boulevard and Bay Road/17th Street intersection.
           There are three signalized intersections along this segment, including the signalized
           intersection at Bay Road with 17th Street. A bus stop and bus bay are located on the
           southwest corner of Purdy Avenue and Dade Boulevard.
           17th Street is an east/west urban minor arterial 0.87 miles long. Within the study limits,
           the segment is a four-lane undivided road from West Avenue to Alton Road, and a two-
           lane undivided from Bay Road to West Avenue. Parking and bicycle lanes are not
           present, but 5-foot sidewalks are present on both sides of 17th Street. The segment
           spans approximately 800 feet (0.15 miles) in length from Bay Road to Alton Road, and
           there are three intersections along this segment.


2.3        Traffic Data
Existing traffic data was collected for the major roadways within the project limits. The data
included turning movement counts (TMCs). Signal timing and phasing data was also obtained
from the Miami-Dade County Public Works Department.


2.3.1      Turning Movement Counts
Turning movement counts were previously collected last year for two hours of each peak period,
which were determined from the average daily traffic volumes (4:00-6:00 PM on a Weekday and
1:30-3:30 PM on a Weekend.) The following locations were included in this study:


      1.   West Avenue and 17th Street (signalized)
      2.   Alton Road and 17th Street (signalized)
      3.   Bay Road and Dade Boulevard (signalized)
      4.   West Avenue and Dade Boulevard (unsignalized)
      5.   Alton Road and Dade Boulevard (signalized)

Additional data collection for this study included turning movement counts at the signalized
intersection of Dade Boulevard and Purdy Avenue. The counts were collected this year on
February 5, 7 and April 9 for the PM peak and on March 8 and April 12 for the weekend peak.
TMC data is included in Appendix B. Figures 3 and 4 illustrate the weekday and weekend
peak hour volumes used in the analysis.

measures of delays, to be used in comparison of alternatives and is summarized in Table 1.
The results of this study were used for calibrating the existing conditions traffic model. The
travel time delay sheets can be found in Appendix C.

2.3.3       Existing Signal Timing Information
Existing signal phasing and timing plans, from the Miami-Dade County Traffic Control Center,
were obtained for the signalized intersection of Dade Boulevard and Purdy Avenue and are
included in Appendix D.


The intersection of Dade Boulevard at Purdy Avenue is signalized and is coordinated in the
east/west direction with Bay Road under Control Section Number 289. The cycle length at this

17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                      Page 12
intersection is 90 seconds on weekdays and weekends. The cycle length at Dade Boulevard at
Bay Road is 110 seconds on weekdays and 90 seconds on weekends.


The intersection of West Avenue at 17th Street is working under Control Section Number 274,
with a cycle length of 82 seconds on weekdays and weekends. This Section also includes the
north-south traffic signals along Alton Road; however, these are operating with a cycle length of
130 seconds on weekdays and weekends.




17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                        Page 13
3.0 EXISTING LEVEL OF SERVICE ANALYSIS

The existing LOS was calculated and analyzed using version (6) of Synchro. Synchro is a traffic
software for modeling and optimizing traffic signal timings. It implements the methods of the
2000 Highway Capacity Manual chapters for Urban Streets, Signalized Intersections and
Unsignalized Intersections. In addition to that, Synchro is capable of calculating the effects of
coordination automatically and accurately.


The analysis of Existing Conditions was assessed by using the accepted measure of
effectiveness for roadway congestion, Level of Service (LOS). LOS "A" describes primarily free-
flow operations at average speeds along an arterial or very low delays at intersections. LOS "F"
describes traffic operations with excessive delay, extremely low speeds and extensive queuing.
LOS "D" (or better) is the desired target to be achieved at both signalized intersections and
corridors. The LOS worksheets are included in Appendix E.


3.1    Intersection Level of Service Analysis

3.1.1      Weekday PM Peak Level of Service
The results of the weekday evening peak hour intersection LOS analysis (of signalized and
unsignalized intersections), are summarized in Table 2.


During the weekday PM peak hour, the results showed that all signalized intersections are
operating at acceptable LOS. Table 2 also indicates that the majority of the failing movements
occur along Alton Road at Dade Boulevard and at 17th Street intersections, in the east/west
direction. The EB right-turn also fails at Dade Boulevard and Bay Road. Only one southbound
movement (SB left-turn) fails at Alton Road and 17th Street intersection.

17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                        Page 17
4.0 PROJECT LEVEL OF SERVICE ANALYSIS

The proposed project would create a bridge over Collins Canal, with an at-grade roadway
intersection between West Avenue and Dade Boulevard. Since the Collins Canal is considered
a non-navigable waterway, except for small crafts, the bridge design would result in a low-level
bridge with minimal vertical clearance similar to the existing bridges at Alton Road and at 17th
Street over the Canal. This bridge would consist of a two-span, concrete flat-slab, skewed
bridge approximately seventy-five feet (75') long. It would accommodate two 12' lanes, a 5'
bicycle lane on each side, a 5' sidewalk on each side with a 1'-1" pedestrian barrier on the
exterior edges, and 1'-6" traffic railing barriers separating the traffic from pedestrian traffic,
requiring approximately 49 feet, 2 inches across the bridge width. Traffic volumes were diverted
along Alton Road at critical intersections to the proposed West Avenue Bridge. Figures 5 and 6
show the project volumes for the weekday and weekend peak periods.


Based on the traffic volume diversion, Level of Service (LOS) Analyses were performed for the
proposed bridge conditions. The project LOS was calculated and analyzed using version (6) of
Synchro. Synchro is a traffic software for modeling and optimizing traffic signal timings. It
implements the methods of the 2000 Highway Capacity Manual chapters for Urban Streets,
Signalized Intersections and Unsignalized Intersections. In addition to that, Synchro is capable
of calculating the effects of coordination automatically and accurately.


The analysis of the proposed project alternative was assessed by using the accepted measure
of effectiveness for roadway congestion, Level of Service (LOS). LOS "A" describes primarily
free-flow operations at average speeds along an arterial or very low delays at intersections.
LOS "F" describes traffic operations with excessive delay, extremely low speeds and extensive
queuing. LOS "D" (or better) is the desired target to be achieved at both signalized intersections
and corridors. The LOS worksheets are included in Appendix F.


The following signal improvements are included under the project scenario:
        West Avenue at 17th Street now operates as a four-leg operation with the proposed
        bridge connection on the SB approach. This intersection is recommended to continue
        operating under Control Section Number 274 and coordinated in the east/west
        direction.
        West Avenue at Dade Boulevard is a new signalized intersection being proposed,
        operating under Control Section Number 274 and coordinated in the east/west direction
        with a cycle length of 130 seconds for both weekday and weekend peak periods.
        Traffic optimization on coordinated sections consisted of holding the existing cycle
        length while optimizing the phasing splits and the offsets.            At uncoordinated
        intersections, optimization consisted of adjusting the phasing splits.

        17th Street ­ As with existing conditions, this link operates with LOS F in both directions
        of travel. These results are also similar to the project weekday conditions.
        Dade Boulevard ­ Similar to existing conditions, the arterial segment is operating
        operates with LOS F and E in the EB and WB directions of travel, respectively.

4.3     Level of Service Comparison
A comparison of the intersection level of service analyses is summarized in Table 10. The LOS
improves slightly with the proposed bridge for the intersections along Dade Boulevard at Bay
Road and at Alton Road during the weekday PM peak hour. However, the LOS slightly
decreases at the intersection along West Avenue at Dade Boulevard and at 17th Street during
both peak periods. This is due to the introduction of the new signal at Dade Boulevard and
West Avenue and the new south approach at West Avenue and 17th Street. Notwithstanding, all
of the intersections are still operating at acceptable levels of service D or better.


                               Table 10. Intersection LOS Comparison
                                    Existing Conditions          Proposed Bridge
              Intersection        Weekday PM     Weekend      Weekday PM   Weekend
        Dade Boulevard
                Purdy Avenue              B             B            B           B
                Bay Road                  D             C            C           C
                West Avenue               A             A            D           D
                Alton Road                D             C            C           C
        17th Street
                West Avenue               B             B            C           C
                Alton Road                D             D            D           D




A comparison of the arterial level of service analyses is summarized in Table 11. As shown in
the summary table, all of the corridor segments are operating below level of service D, except
for the segment of Dade Boulevard in the westbound direction under existing conditions during
the weekday PM peak hour. The LOS improves slightly with the proposed bridge for the
segment of Dade Boulevard in the westbound direction during the weekend peak hour from a
LOS F to E. However, it is the reverse for the weekday PM peak hour, with the LOS decreasing
from D to F under the proposed bridge scenario. The LOS also decreases slightly from E to F
with the proposed bridge for Dade Boulevard in the eastbound direction during both peak
periods.

                  Westbound           F             F            F           F

Several conceptual improvements were developed in order to improve operations at the critical
intersections along both east-west corridors. The improvements were considered for both
existing conditions and with the proposed West Avenue Bridge project. In developing the
improvements, geometric constraints as well traffic volumes and movements were taken into
account. The following roadway and intersection improvements were considered:

17th Street/Dade Boulevard Corridor Study - DRAFT                                                   Page 26
6.0 CONCLUSIONS

The purpose of the study was to evaluate the traffic operations of the east-west corridors of 17th
Street and Dade Boulevard and to develop potential conceptual improvements in the traffic flow
and roadway connectivity for the critical intersections within the study limits. This study also
assessed the impacts that the proposed bridge connection at West Avenue would have on the
intersection of Dade Boulevard and Purdy Avenue.


The study entailed data collection, an existing conditions analysis, and an analysis of the
proposed bridge connection at West Avenue. The traffic analysis also considered the impacts
to the surrounding neighborhood from routing some of the traffic from Alton Road to West
Avenue, a local street.

Based on the data collection and the analysis performed, the results indicate that the proposed
bridge crossing alone does not greatly improve the traffic operations for the east-west corridors.
Additional improvements consisting of modifications to the existing bridge and other critical
intersections will need to be evaluated further in order to maximize the benefits of the proposed
bridge.


In addition, safety for pedestrians and bicyclists, as well as vehicular traffic, may be improved
with the proposed bridge. A safety review of the critical intersections along Dade Boulevard
should be made in order to determine the extent of these benefits more accurately. Also, the
right-of-way requirements, as well as the roadway alignment, need to be evaluated further for
the east-west corridors. A benefit/cost analysis would also need to be conducted in order to
quantify the benefits of the proposed bridge connection for the east-west corridors.


A previous benefit/cost analysis, which evaluated the north-south corridors of West Avenue and
Alton Road, indicated that the construction of the proposed bridge was economically feasible.
Furthermore, the proposed bridge will provide a more direct connection to the Sunset
Neighborhood.
